E-mail: ul@library.oauife.edu.ng|http://library.oauife.edu.ng||||I hereby authorize the Hezekiah Oluwasanmi Library to copy my thesis in whole or in part in response to request from individual researchers and organizations for the purpose of private study or research|The need to diversify the economic base, and also increase the foreign earning capacity of the country forms the main objectives for tourism development in Nigeria.  The potentialities for tourism in Nigeria are many, but her tourism resources are yet to be fully developed.  The success of the tourism sector in this country has continuously been hampered by the general lack of primary infrastructures and services needed for tourism and a weak organizational machinery.  The totality of these shortcomings makes tourism a fertile but fallow sector, despite the comparatively huge investments in Nigeria.In this study the methodology involved relevant literature review, carrying out sample survey by questionnaire and analyzing the data collected.  Past efforts to develop tourism in Ondo State have been largely concentrated on the development of Ikogosi Warm Spring which is the focus of this study.  Measures taken to develop other tourist attraction centres, which fortunately abound in the state, amount to piece-meal.  In addition to the lack of primary infrastructural facilities in the existing tourist centres, there is also a dearth of trained personnel, substandard hotels and associated services, and poor transport facilities.Despite the greater attention focused on the development of Ikogosi Warm Spring, the achievements of the centre still fall short of expectations.  Efforts, so far, have been concentrated on the development of chalets, most of which are under utilized, while neglecting other relevant facilities and services like electricity, water supply and catering.The various steps taken in the past are not sufficient to achieve the required standard for tourism in the state.  It is necessary therefore, to prepare a Master Plan for tourism development in the state and evolve a tourism policy with the aim of upgrading, evaluating and effectively promoting tourism in and outside the state.  Due consideration for the provision of adequate facilities, utilities and an effective promotional strategy is recommended at the end of this study for proper development of the tourist centres in Ondo State.|Theses collection|Tourism development in Nigeria/Tourism resources*||||||Moro, Dauphin  Dighitoghi|Male|A study of bacterial species of the endocervix of infertile and fertile women attending fertility clinic in Ile - Ife.||||||M. Sc. Microbiology|K. A. Ako-Nai, F. E. Okonofua||Ile-Ife|Obafemi Awolowo University, Microbiology|1993|||OAU|||||viii, 138p.|||||||English||Obafemi Awolowo University, H. O. Library, Ile-Ife, Osun State. E-mail: ul@library.oauife.edu.ng|http://library.oauife.edu.ng||||I hereby authorize the Hezekiah Oluwasanmi Library to copy my thesis in whole or in part in response to request from individual researchers and organizations for the purpose of private study or research|Several studies have shown the microbial flora of the female genital tract. Both the vagina and cervix harbour various microorganisms. Endocervical colonization by pathogens have been reported to cause morbidity of the reproductive system which may result in infertility and congenital malformation in the foetus. Information relating to endocervical microflora of Nigerian women is scarce in the literature hence this study. The objectives of the study are : isolation and identification of microbes in the endocervix of infertile and pregnant women in Ile-Ife, determination and comparison of host factors contributing to microbial colonization and determination of the in-vitro antibiotic susceptibility pattern of the isolates.Endocervical cultures from one hundred and seventy eight women consisting of 92 infertile and 86 pregnant women were processed. The primary isolation media used were blood agar, eosin-methylene blue agar, mannitol salt agar, sabouraud dextrose agar, Thayer-Martin agar, brain heart infusion broth and cooked meat medium. The isolates were identified based on cultural, morphological and biochemical characteristics. Wet mount and direct Gram's stain of each endocervical swab was also made on clean glass slides for microscopy. Antibiotic susceptibility pattern of bacteria was determined by the disc diffusion method while the medical histories of participants were obtained from their case notes and questionnaire method was also used. Data were statistically analysed using the Chi-square technique.A total of three hundred and sixty seven microbial isolates were recovered with 203 (55.3%) from the infertile women and 164 (44.7%) from the pregnant.  Forty six percent of the total bacterial isolates from the infertile women and forty-eight percent of those from the pregnant women were pathogens.  These included Neisseria gonorrhoeae which constituted 19.7%, Staphylococcus aureus, 18.7%, beta haemolytic streptococci 4.4% and Clostridium sp, 3.9% of the isolates cultured from the infertile women.   Similarly, N. gonorrhoeae was recovered from 17%, S. aureus 14.6%, beta haemolytic streprococci 10.4% and Clostridium sp 6.1% of the total isolates from the pregnant women.  Other organism isolated were Pseudomonas aeruginosa, Proteus vulgaris, Escherichia coli, Haemophilus sp, Bacillus sp, coagulase negative staphylococci (CONS), Candida sp and Trichomonas vaginalis.  Similar organisms were cultured from both groups of women.The result showed that 17.5% of the infertile women from whom N. gonorrhoeae was isolated had history of pelvic inflammatory disease (PID), 10% had history of bilateral tubal occlusion (BTO) and 2.5% with cervicitis.  Similarly, 10.5% of the infertile women from whom S. aureus were cultured had PID, 13.2%, BTO and 5.3% cervicitis.  Altogether, 68 (73.9%) of the infertile women had secondary infertility which was about three times more frequent compared to 24 (26.1%) with primary infertility.  The bacteria cultured from their endocervix showed multiple antibiotic resistance to commonly employed antibiotics.  The study revealed bacterial colonization of the endocervix of infertile and pregnant women with pathogens specifically N. gonorrhoeae which is of concern to their neonates particularly those delivered through the birth canal.  The study also revealed the prevalence of antibiotic resistant organisms among the participants.|Theses collection|Bacterial species/bacterial species of the endocervix of infertile and fertile women*||||||Akinwole, Philips Olugbemiga|Male |Microenvironmental preferences of soil dwelling mites on the floor of a secondary regrowth forest in Ile-Ife||||||M. Sc. Zoology|M. A. Badejo||Ile-Ife|Obafemi Awolowo University, Zoology|2004|||OAU|||||xi, 87p.|||||||English||Obafemi Awolowo University, H. O. Library, Ile-Ife, Osun State. E-mail: ul@library.oauife.edu.ng|http://library.oauife.edu.ng||||I hereby authorize the Hezekiah Oluwasanmi Library to copy my thesis in whole or in part in response to request from individual researchers and organizations for the purpose of private study or research|The major objective of this study was to determine the species composition of the soil dwelling mites living under the different microenvironments on a forest floor at Obafemi Awolowo University Campus, Ile Ife. This is to know the possible influence of moisture content and temperature on the different species as well as to determine the seasonal variation in the age structure of each species. The work also aimed at breeding selected groups of the mites in the laboratory so as to know their feeding preference.Sampling was done monthly from August 2002 to April 2003 covering the two seasons of the annual cycle. On each sampling occasion, soil samples were taken from three layers of the topsoil from four subplots of a 25 m2 marked out from each of two contrasting habitats (shaded and unshaded area) on the forest floor. Litter samples were collected within a 25 x 25 cm quadrat below which the fermentation and topsoil samples were taken using a soil auger. The soil and litter samples were collected in polythene bags, labeled and brought to the laboratory. Site-specific data on rainfall, soil moisture contents, and soil temperature were simultaneously collected. The samples were extracted for microarthropods in the Berlesse Tullgreen extractor. The mites were later identified to genera or species level and sorted from the rest of the microarthropods under a stereo dissecting microscope. Some of the mites were extracted alive and later used for the breeding experiment.There was an overwhelming predominance of mite populations in the 5 cm topsoil where peak populations reached 54,000 mites per m2 in October 2002, compared with the fermentation and litter layers where peak populations were 7,500 mites per m2 in February 2003 and 12,500 mites per m2 in August 2002 respectively. Microenvironmental differences in the shaded and unshaded plots were reported to have influenced the densities and fluctuation patterns of the mite populations. The large numbers of mites extracted from the topsoil in the shaded plot was attributed to highly conducive moisture conditions provided by the canopy. It was observed that Mesoplophora ifeana had preference for moist conditions during the dry and wet seasons, while Mixacarus spp. appeared to prefer fairly moist condition. Therelatively stable population of M. ifeana and Scheloribates mochlosimilaris in the fermentation layer is a consequence of many interacting microenvironmental factors which include rainfall and temperature.The feeding of members of Polyaspidae and Teleolides on the algae Pleurococcus sp., indicates that they are algivorous browsers. The pteromorphs, namely, S. mochlosimilaris and M inexpectata fed on the yeast and litter filtrate (panphytophagous) and were present in all the three soil layers investigated. It was observed that the active feeding of Pergalumna and Teleolides was responsible for their relatively longer survival in the laboratory when compared with the other taxonomic groups. The rejection of food by Actinedida and Uropodidae suggests that they could be predators or carrion feeders.The study concluded that canopy cover affected the sensitivity of soil dwelling mites on the floor of a secondary regrowth forest with regard to vertical gradients of light, microclimate and foliage quality in a complex way.|Theses collection|Soil dwelling mites / Secondary regrowth forest*||||||Obong, Inyang Akpan|Male|Dairy factory complex: design proposal for Obudu cattle ranch Cross River State||||||M. Sc. Applied  Geology|O. S. Adegoke,  E. I. Enu||Ile-Ife|Obafemi Awolowo University,|1984|||OAU|||||272p.|||||||English||Obafemi Awolowo University, H. O. Library, Ile-Ife, Osun State. E-mail: ul@library.oauife.edu.ng|http://library.oauife.edu.ng||||I hereby authorize the Hezekiah Oluwasanmi Library to copy my thesis in whole or in part in response to request from individual researchers and organizations for the purpose of private study or research|The evolution of the Dahomey basin began in Pre-Cretaceous time. The proto-Dahomey depocentre was a simple downwarped faulted basin. The deposits constitute part of a larger West African -Brazilian intercratonic sedimentary sequence.The inception of the basin is related to the tensional forces that culminated in the separation of the African plate from the South American plate. Tectonism was mainly controlled by Mesozoic fracture zones and faults, such as the Chain, Romanche and Charcot Fracture Zones.The geology is dominated by a series of parallel to Subparallel faults, trending in a northeast to southwest direction. Vertical displacements led to the developmentof horst and grabens which controlled sedimentation. Sediment cover is moderated thick and there are no evidences of metamorphism or volcanism. The basin is thus a miogeosynclinal type. The sedimentary record is complicated by the occurrence of many unconformities and hiatuses.Sedimentation was syntectonic. Various postdrift episodes of transgression and regression were well preserved. The sediments are mainly classics, ranging from conglomerates and through sands and limestones to shales and marls.Geophysical evidences show that the sediments pinch out against the Basement Complex. This makes the Cretaceous sands (Afowo Formation) a good target for oil exploration,since it is overlain by the shaley  Araromi Formation, a possible cap rock.The fact that heavy oil and tar had been discovered in the Nigerian sector and high grade light crude in the offshore of the Benin Republic suggest a possible occurrence of light crude in the offshore of the Nigerian sectorDitch cutting samples studied yielded 50 species of Foraminifera including 6 new species. The three newly erected Cretaceous formations of Omatsola and Adegoke (1981) were characterised for the first time with their responses on geophysical logs.A model for the tectonic evolution of the Dahomey Basin is proposed.|Theses collection|Dahomey Basin*||||||Afolayan, S. Funsho.|Male|Igbomina under colonial rule 1900-1960||||||M. A. History|A. A. Adediran||Ile-Ife, Nigeria|Obafemi Awolowo University,  History|1984|||OAU|||||vii, 145p.|||||||English||Obafemi Awolowo University, H. O. Library, Ile-Ife, Osun State. E-mail: ul@library.oauife.edu.ng|http://library.oauife.edu.ng||||I hereby authorize the Hezekiah Oluwasanmi Library to copy my thesis in whole or in part in response to request from individual researchers and organizations for the purpose of private study or research|This study focuses on Igbomina under colonial rule.  It provides as a baseline, information on the pre-colonial Igbomina society, especially on those institutions that the British either built upon and used or destroyed.  Pre-colonial Igbomina was under the suzerainty of the Fulani who were operating the Ijia (District Head) system of government from Ilorin and Lafiagi.  This arrangement was incorporated and adapted by the British.  The system, hitherto oppressive, became even more oppressive during the colonial period.	The operation of this system was further reinforced by the colonial disregard for traditional practices, the trampling on, and undermining of, the powers of traditional rulers.  This, coupled with the colonial economic exploitation, generated hostile reactions in Igbomina.  The result was riots, agitation for the creation of more local governments and a call for independence from foreign rule.  Attempts by the British to solve one crisis only produced others.  This chain reaction continued until 1960 when the country attained independence.	The colonial period, however, witnessed a number of socio-economic changes in the ways of life of the people: roads were constructed, schools and hospitals were built and a new religion, Christianity, was successfully introduced.|Theses collection|Igbomina under colonial rule*||||||Ajayi, Gabriel Oladipupo.|Male|A design proposal for general post office, Akure.||||||M. It is hypothesized that except for the very few who are privileged with secondary or higher education, the educational status of females is improving only slightly. This study therefore, investigated the effects of some family characteristics (mainly family structural variables) on female educational aspirations in Oyo State secondary schools of Nigeria.Three hundred and fifty nine female secondary school students drawn from six randomly chosen local government areas of Oyo State were involved in the study. Data were collected with the use of questionnaires.  Both descriptive and inferential statistics were used in the analysis.About one-quarter of the respondents were found to be of low educational aspirations, while seventy percent of them had medium level of aspiration and about five percent had high aspirations. Positive significant relationships were round between the female students' educational aspirations and parental levels of education., types of occupation, fathers' material possession scores, sisters' levels of educational attainments and the students' scholastic performances Both fathers' and mothers' levels of education have almost equal positive effects on the students' aspirations. However the fathers' types of occupation seem to be a more important factor for the students' educational aspirations.Family size, number of wives in the family and students' ages were also found to have significant negative correlations with the students' educational aspirations. Students' order of birth although negatively correlated was not significant. There were also significant differences between the urban and rural family students in their scholastic performances and educational aspirations.On the basis of the findings, it was recommended that there should be deliberate governmental interventions to raise rural dwellers levels of living. Areas of further research were also identified.|Theses collection|Family Characteristics / Female Educationa*|||||| Akande, Sili. In the first few years of independence, three areas of external relations received emphasis  the Commonwealth, the OAU and the United Nations. When Nigeria joined the Commonwealth in 1960, it was optimistic about its usefulness, hoping to benefit diplomatically and economically.However events after 1960, as this study shows, betrayed this optimism. But for the successful struggle  in 1961 for the expulsion of South Africa from the Commonwealth, other aspirations were unfulfilled; there were little or no economic advantages; the body did not do much to help Zimbabwe in the struggle for independence and Nigeria witnessed a civil war which Commonwealth members failed to resolve.By 1970, the relationship with the Commonwealth was being assessed, not by the government, which still preferred membership, but by the people who pointed out the ineffectiveness of the organisation. The muchtalked about machinery for consultation was not of much use, as Britain, the core of the association, continued to act as she deemed fit, even when opinion in the Commonwealth ran counter to her actions. It was also pointed out that during the civil war in Nigeria  the body could not reach a common line of action. Finally, as an economic body, it did not prove itself a useful organisation.|Theses collection| Nigeria and  the Commonwealth                                                                                                                                               *||||||Adegoke Sola Adetunla.|Male|Advertising in a television media ||||||MBA Business Administration|John Weinrich||Ile-Ife, Nigeria|Obafemi Awolowo University, Management and Accounting|1981|||OAU|||||ix, 133p.|||||||English||Obafemi Awolowo University, H. The researcher compared the quality of the curricula which apprentices inboth systems were exposed to by evaluating the quality of copies of matchets made by the apprentices when they were given prototype matchets. Three hypotheses were raised to compare the skills of formally and non-formally trained apprentices;1)	on precision at copying;2)	material selection; and3)	qualities of end-product.Students of the Technical Colleges of Oyo and OwO respectively constituted the formally trained apprentices, while blacksmith apprentices randomly selected in Oyo and Ondo States constituted their non-formally trained counter parts. The subjects were given a made in Birmingham matchet each to copy and reproduce. Matchets produced by both groups were scored. The 't' test analysis of the performances of the two groups at level 0.01, df 48, yielded the following results for skills in:-1)	copying precisely tc = 14.83 > tt = 2.68;2)	material selection tc = 17.82 > tt = 2.68; and3)	finesse of end-product tc = 23.89 > tt = 2,68. The differences were significant in favour of the non-formally trained apprentices. It follows therefore that: Non-formally trained apprentices performed better in all the skills tested than their counterparts in formal institutions. The study reveals that the curriculum offered by non-formal (traditional) apprenticeship system is more effective than that offered by formal apprenticeship system. A lasting solution to it will involve obtaining a fairly balanced development between the rural communities and urban centres, by the provision of amenities such as Educational, Social and Cultural facilities, as well as employment opportunities, in the rural areas.A well composed and functional community centre with other associated amenities will provide most of these required facilities and employment opportunities in the community.To produce a functional community centre, the justification for it in this area, Amichi, and its possible integration into the culture was carried out through a review of literature on the town and environs, the people and culture, government policies on such centres, and oral interviews with a cross section of the people (users) and community leaders (clients).Furthermore, a critical appraisal of some existing community centres within and outside the country was done in order to establish standards, forms, spatial composition and managerial efficiency which form the guidelines for the design proposal.Then, to ensure, proper integration of the designproposal of a court-yard concept for the COMMUNITY CENTRE FOR AMICHI, which in its functional context and spatial composition, would provide public facilities for the education and the entertainment of the community. Many strategies based on the philosophy of seismic wave propagation in various complex geological environments are employed in practical schemes, often referred to as algorithms, for deconvolution.A number of deconvolution schemes namely Wiener, Kalman, Homomorphic and Minimum Entropy have been reviewed in this study. A detailed study of Wiener least squares filter has led to a modified filter development based on the minimization of the least squares error and a more efficient desired output. Various examples are given to illustrate this development. The objective was to investigate the extent to which principals actually performed their roles (instructional, administration, human relations) as perceived by their reference groups (teachers, students) and principals themselves.The instrument used in the study was a thirty-item questionnaire tagged "Principals' Roles Perception and Performance Questionnaire (PRPPQ)". This questionnaire was designed to elicit responses of teachers, students and principals' perception and performance on principals roles in three functional areas, namely; instructional, administrative and human relations. A total of five hundred and sixty respondents, made up of 35 principals, 175 teachers and 350 students from 35 randomly selected secondary schools were interviewed. The data collected were analysed using descriptive statistics.The results showed that the principals were qualified and experienced and exhibited high level of effective performance in administrative and human relation roles as compared to instructional roles. Specific remedial packages were also constructed to enable subjects who were deficient in certain areas of each weeks work to remediate for such deficiencies.  The subjects concerned used the specific remedial packages as self learning devices. The subjects in the SFR group cultivated a more positive attitude towards physics than the subjects in the SFO and the CM groups as revealed by ANOVA test (P < 0.01). The para-substituents were classified into electron-donating (for P-NH2, P-CH3 CONH, and P-CH3 substituents) and electron-withdrawwing groups (for the P-NO2 substituents).	Substrate-surfactant interactions occur particularly above the critical micelle concentration (CMC) of the surface-active agent.  The effect of this interaction on the hydolysis rate, whether it is an increase or decrease in rate, or no effect may depend on the orientation of the substrate in the micelle, and on the surfactant type and concentration.  Although the presence of different para-substituents have been reported to influence the effect of CTAB on the hydrolysis rate of a number of esters, reports being presented are not in agreement with the literature information.	Using the various para-substituted sulfonyl fluorides did not result in inhibition (in the case of electron-denoting groups) or catalysis (in the case of derivatives with electron-withdrawing groups).  Instead of the expected result, inhibition was observed in all cases.	The kinetic results were analysed using the multi-plot approach.  This analysis clearly indicated that the various substituents were appreciably partitioned into the micellar phase.  Furthermore, the results showed that the various substituents did not determine the degree of micellar stabilization.	Thus, with the sulfonyl fluoride/CTAB system, the extent of interaction may be a primary factor in determining the type of effect observed, instead of the electron activity of the various para substituents.|Theses collection|cationic surfactant / alkaline hydrolysis / benzene sulfonyl fluorides*||||||Ikotun, Titilola Janet|Female|An analysis of the effect of pre and post organizer on the teaching and learning of biological concepts||||||M. Heat units as defined by method 7 which used the daily mean temperature above a base of 15.5 C was not better than calendar days in five of ten cultivars.  It could be concluded therefore that heat units as defined by a method may not be better than calendar days if the structure of the computing heat unit equation is not much related to the true effects of the prevailing temperatures on growth, in a particular environment.  Evaluation of the 12 heat unit methods on the basis of coefficient of variability and correlation and regression analyses showed that the best heat unit method for predicting silking dates under the hot tropical rain forest location of this study was method 9 which uses an optimum temperature of 30 C and a base temperature of 10 C. E-mail: ul@library.oauife.edu.ng|http://library.oauife.edu.ng||||I hereby authorize the Hezekiah Oluwasanmi Library to copy my thesis in whole or in part in response to request from individual researchers and organizations for the purpose of private study or research|The administration of chloroquine and aspirin to pregnant Wister rats at specific periods of gestation was demonstrated to be teratogenic.  Both chloroquine and aspirin caused degenerative processes in the placenta.  Chloroquine, its polar and non-polar metabolites were demonstrated in the blood and urine of the mother animals whereas only chloroquine and its non-polar metabolites were demonstrated in the fetuses.	Teratogenic activities of chloroquine and aspirin were greatest when the drugs were administered from the 1st to the 10th days of gestation with a peak during the period 6th to the 10th day.  The administration of chloroquine and aspirin to pregnant Wister rats significantly caused a reduction in the litter size, live births and birth weights; whilst it produced significant increase in the intra-uterine and neonatal deaths among the experimental groups.  The greatest significant effects were on the reduction of live birth and increase in the intra-uterine death.	Chloroquine administered to pregnant Wister rats caused varied morphological abnormalities which were first identified during the gestational period 6th to 10th day.  These abnormalities included haemangioma of the brain, deficient calcification of the cranium, spinal-bifida, deficient skeletal calcification, cleft palate and lips, opacity of the lens and cornea, exophthalmia and foetal runts.  Aspirin administration to pregnant Wister rats caused morphological abnormalities in the fetuses which included haemangioma of the brain, deficient calcification of the cranium and phecomelia of both upper and lower limbs.	Administration of chloroquine and aspirin resulted in synergistic reaction with aspirin potentiating the teratogenic action of chloroquine.  Prolonged administration of chloroquine, aspirin, or the combination of the two drugs to pregnant Wister rats was incompatible with foetal viability.	The clinical implications of these findings with reference to chloroquine medication during pregnancy is emphasized.	Recommendations are made for further studies on chloroquine to establish the mechanism of its teratogenicity and to clinically confirm or disprove the extrapolation of these teratogenic effects in man in view of the importance of chemotherapy with chloroquine in man.	|Theses collection|Teratogenic / Chloroquine / Aspirin / Rat *||||||Adesulu, Isaac Olufemi|Male|Management structure in a quasi-governmental industrial concern: Nigerian-Romanian wood industries limited (NIROWI)||||||M. Mn content ranged from 9.1 mg/kg in maize to 145 mg/kg in oyster shell; Ca ranged from 0.03% in maize to 37.5% in oyster shell; and P ranged from 0.01% in palm oil to 14.12% in bone meal.  In general, the commonly used energy sources had lower Ca, P and Mn levels than protein and mineral sources.  The latter were as expected, the richest source of these minerals.	The biological availability of the three elements (Ca, P and Mn) in representative samples of the above three classes of feeds was determined in broilers, using a simple mineral balance technique that made correction for endogenous minerals excretion.  The bio-availability to broilers of the three minerals were: maize (53.9, 40.8, 64.2); ground nut cake (71.1, 59.1, 64.1); fish meal (89.4, 90.4, 93.7); bone meal (94.6, 88.1, 81.3); oyster shell (96.5, 90.6, 99.3) for percent Ca, P and Mn respectively.  Availability of Mn from MnSO4 was 99%.	A factorial design with 3 levels of Ca (0.9, 1.9, 2.9%) and 2 levels of P (0.6, 1.2%) was employed to study the effects of high dietary Ca and P on Mn utilization in broilers.  The level of dietary Mn was 70 mg/kg diet.  Only dietary P had significant effect on broiler performance and mortality, with high dietary P (1.2%) depressing (P<.01) weight gain and efficiency of feed utilization and causing a higher ( P<.01) mortality rate.  The trend was different for parameters on bone characteristics, perosis score and Mn status of the birds for which Ca and P interaction effects were significant (P<.01).  High dietary Ca tended to distrupt Mn metabolism, causing high and severe incidence of perosis and low tibia Mn.  High dietary P attenuated the distruptive effects of high dietary Ca on Mn metabolism. 	Another experiment was carried out to quantify the upward adjustments of dietary Mn required to correct the hazards of dietary Ca and P interaction effect on Mn metabolism.  A total of 150 Cobb-broilers divided into 5 groups of 30 each were fed 5 diets containing increasing levels of Mn (77.5, 140, 200, 255, 300 mg/kg) but similar Ca (2.9%) and P (0.6%) levels for 6 weeks.  Increasing dietary Mn from 77.5 up to and including 200 mg/kg, raised (P<.01) the Mn levels in tibia and feathers and reduced (P<.01) the incidence and severity of perosis.  Above 200 mg/kg diet, there were no additional benefit from the added dietary Mn, suggesting that the detrimental effect of a diet with Ca: P ratio as wide as 4.8:1 on Mn utilization can be controlled by increasing dietary Mn to 200 mg/kg.  A study of the apparent biological availability of Mn in broilers, revealed that the Mn availability fell (P<.01) from 46.3% when dietary Mn was 77.5 mg/kg to 31.1% at the highest dietary Mn level of 300 mg/kg.  Correlation coefficient between dietary Mn and availability was -0.98. ||Calcium, phos phorus and manganese interactions in the aetiology of perosis in broilers*||||||Ekpe, Samuel Eni|Male|An economic analysis of the national accelerated fish production project : a case study of the UTA Ewa Pilot Project||||||M. O. Library, Ile-Ife, Osun State. E-mail: ul@library.oauife.edu.ng|http://library.oauife.edu.ng||||I hereby authorize the Hezekiah Oluwasanmi Library to copy my thesis in whole or in part in response to request from individual researchers and organizations for the purpose of private study or research|This dissertation is the first step towards a more comprehensive work in African aesthetic; hence the focus is on the analysis and clarification of basic aesthetic issues, position and arguments.  The objective is to examine the current arguments in African aesthetics and to identify those theoretically important issues whose resolutions will greatly enrich the discipline.  In pursuance of this objective, the dissertation starts with the exposition and assessment of the main relativists positions in aesthetics.  It examines the issues between the relativist and the universalist and arrives at the conclusion that the anti-universalist and anti-objectivist claims of the relativist rests upon a mistake.  The mistake is the supposition that aesthetic values, concepts and standards are unique to each culture.	Although the dissertation agrees that there is a correlation of aesthetic values with their historical context, it holds that this should not be construed as an evidence that aesthetic values are unique to their culture in any special sense.  Otherwise, the relativist has to show that it is impossible for the aesthetic values of one culture to be exemplified in another.  The position which this dissertation defends is that aesthetic values do not express some definite aesthetic characteristic unique to a particular culture; rather, they exemplify socio-historical conditions.  Hence given similar aesthetic and cultural situations, the same type of aesthetic value will result.	The dissertation concludes by noting the consequences of the relativists theoretical inadequacies on the question of understanding African aesthetics.|Theses collection|African aesthetics / relativism*||||||Ogungbenro, Basiru Mosobalaje|Male|The efficiency of transmission of three isolates of pepper veinal mottle virus by the green peach aphid (myzus persicae sulz.) and the groundnut aphid (aphis craccivora koch.)||||||M.Sc. E-mail: ul@library.oauife.edu.ng|http://library.oauife.edu.ng||||I hereby authorize the Hezekiah Oluwasanmi Library to copy my thesis in whole or in part in response to request from individual researchers and organizations for the purpose of private study or research|Indigofera pulchra Willd. is a widely distributed, readily grazed, wild perennial herbaceous legume.  It is able to continue active growth and nodulation in the critical period of the dry season when other herbs are dry and quiescent.  It is abundant in soils very low in nitrogen and organic matter.	Three distinct morphological forms are here recognized: a simple-leaved form; a simple-compound-leaved form and a compound-leaved form.	Nitrogen concentrations in the leaves, stem and roots are significantly different within and between the forms.  One form, Jos 1 compound-leaved, appeared to have a different growth rate, and seed germination character also varies among the forms.	The distributions of I. pulchra, grass tussocks and other legumes were found never to be random but to show various scales of contagion.  The local pattern of I. pulchra distribution is largely controlled by grass tussocks and topography (ridging), which are correlated with soil organic matter concentration (and presumably cation exchange capacity and nitrogen concentration).  I. pulchra was found not to be able to compete with tall grasses.	Seeds were treated in concentrated sulphuric acid, boiling water, tap water and by scarification.  The acid treatment gave the highest percentage germination (70  100%) while tap water treatment gave the lowest, (0  1%).	The suggestion is made that I. pulchra can be utilized by seeding into infertile open savanna areas and into managed ranges.  The Jos 1 compound-leaved form is suggested as the most suitable for further investigation and field trials.|Theses collection|indigofera pulchra wild *||||||Badifu, Gabriel Ijegbunam Okei|Male|Evaluation of  'OGI' from red and white sorghum||||||M. Geology|A. A. Kayode||Ile - Ife, Nigeria|Obafemi Awolowo University,|1984|||OAU|||||xxii, 370p.|||||||English||Obafemi Awolowo University, H. O. Library, Ile-Ife, Osun State. E-mail: ul@library.oauife.edu.ng|http://library.oauife.edu.ng||||I hereby authorize the Hezekiah Oluwasanmi Library to copy my thesis in whole or in part in response to request from individual researchers and organizations for the purpose of private study or research|The Igbeti area is within the Pre-cambrian Basement Complex of southwestern Nigeria and is situated to the east of the West African Craton.  Rocks of the area include (i) Hornblende-biotite and augen gneisses (ii) the younger metasediments consisting of mica-schist, quartzites, dolomitic marble and amphibolites and (iii) fine to medium grained and the coarse to coarse porphyritic granites which are intrusive into the metamorphic rocks.	A total of 210 representative samples of the various rock units were studied petrographically and analysed for both major and trace elements contents.  The hornblende-biotite gneiss is geochemically characterized by high values of CaO + Na20 (average = 6.76%), low average K2O (2.23%) and high Na20/K2O ratio (average = 1.70) all of which suggest its derivation from a greywacke-like parent rock.	Petrographic observations on the augen gneiss together with its geochemical characteristics, particularly the low K/Rb ration (average = 171), the high K20 + Na20 (average = 7.75%), the high K2O/Na2O ratio (average = 3.35) and the high average Rb/Sr ratio (3.76) as compared to the corresponding and respective values in the hornblende-biotite gneiss and the crust suggest strong overprints of metasomatic effects on the original rock which could have been a biotite gneiss.	Though texturally different, the Igbeti granites are generally calc-alkali to weakly alkali in composition, show strong indications of genetic relationships and were probably emplaced at PH2O below 10 K bars.  Their average K/Rb (208), Rb/Sr (0.68), Ba/Sr (2.29), Ba/Rb (3.53), K/Ba (67.73) ratios and Sr87/Sr86 = 0.7120 + 0.0016 of the Igbeti granites suggest crustal affinity hence it is proposed that the granite magma is of lower crustal origin but with complex evolutionary history.	The alkali feldspar geochemistry, field relationships and other geochemical characteristics of the granites indicate that the magma was highly viscous, poor in volatiles, slightly differentiated and was not markedly contaminated by the surrounding rocks.|Theses collection|Igbeti Granite Complex Oyo State, Nigeria*||||||Odubanjo, Cordelia Olatokunbo|Male|Optimum housing for low-/middle-income Nigerians (Oyo State) : the growth factor||||||M. The chi-square analysis was used to determine the significance of the relationships.The teachers perceived their principals' leadership styles as transactional, (43.19%, 21 principals), democratic, (30.68%, 6 principals), autocratic, (13.50%, 3 principals), pseudo-democratic, (9.79%, 1 principal), and laissez-faire, (2.12%, 1 principal).Teachers' job performances were classified into positive, negative, and neutral types. Plant Science|C. M. McKell||Ile-Ife, Nigeria|Obafemi Awolowo University,|1965|||OAU|||||viii, 80p.|||||||English||Obafemi Awolowo University, H. O. Library, Ile-Ife, Osun State. E-mail: ul@library.oauife.edu.ng|http://library.oauife.edu.ng||||I hereby authorize the Hezekiah Oluwasanmi Library to copy my thesis in whole or in part in response to request from individual researchers and organizations for the purpose of private study or research|This research was carried out in three phases. The first study concerned the effects of top dressing nitrogen at three rates (0, 100, and 250 lb. per acre applied at six-week intervals) on the carbohydrate content of leaves, stems and stolons, roots and rhizomes of coastal Bermudagrass. Plant tissues were analysed for reducing (glucose and fructose}, non-reducing (sucrose) sugars, and for fructosans every two weeks during 1963.The reducing sugar content of leaves increased with increasing rates of fertilization. In stems and stolons as well as in roots and rhizomes no significant changes occurred in reducing sugar content throughout the growth-season. In the leaves there were no significant differences in content of sucrose and fructosan due to fertilizer application but in stems and stolons as well as in rhizomes and roots, sucrose and fructosan content decreased with increasing fertilization.Bermudagrass fertilized at the high rate apparently retains most of the newly synthesized carbohydrate as reducing sugar in-the leaves. The amount of carbohydrate translocated into rhizomes at the high nitrogen level is a small fraction of the total amount synthesized. During the active growth phase, sucrose may be equally as important a source of reserve for regrowth as fructosan.The second phase of the project concerned the evaluation of regrowth potential of the plots fertilized during the first study. Six-inch diameter sod plugs were taken from each plot, put in cans, and grown in a dark chamber. The regrowth potential was measured in mg of dry matter produced per sod plug.The first six-week regrowth was closely related to the content of carbohydrate reserve present in the stubble and rhizome. Sod plugs from plots fertilized at 500 lb. N per acre made the best regrowth. The least regrowth was made by sod plugs from plots fertilized at 750 and 1000 lb. N per acre.The final phase of work involved an evaluation of forage quality of coastal Bermudagrass hays from plots fertilized at 0, 100, and 250 lb. N per acre every six weeks. Rabbits were used as test animals. The grass hays replaced the 40% alfalfa hay normally incorporated into the control ration. Three feeding experiments were carried out using three successive hay harvests. Feed evaluations were based on the live weight gains of young rabbit from age 21 days to 52 days. In the third experiment 8-week-old rabbits were used and the grass feeds were supplemented with preformed vitamin A.In the first two feeding experiments, alfalfa ration was superior to the three coastal Bermudagrass rations, possibly due to the former's higher content of carotene and low level of nitrate. The rabbits fed Bermudagrass rations showed acute symptoms of vitamin A deficiency, masking any observable differences between the coastal Bermudagrass feeds. In the third experiment, rabbits on fertilized Bermudagrass rations performed very poorly. These rations contained levels of nitrate-nitrogen that are possibly toxic to rabbits, and which might interfere with availability and utilization of vitamin A.|Theses collection|Nitrogen fertilization / Carbohydrate content, forage quality and regrowth potential of coastal bermudagrass (cynodon dactylon, (l) pers.)*||||||Eze, Josiah Onyinye|Male|Limited chymotryptic cleavage of archachatina (calachatina) marginata haemocyanin||||||M. The first study concerned the effects of top dressing nitrogen at three rates (0, 100, and250 lb. per acre applied at six-week intervals) on the carbohydrate content of leaves, stems and stolons, roots and rhizomes of coastal Bermudagrass. Plant tissues were analysed for reducing (glucose and fructose), non-reducing (sucrose) sugars, and for fructosans every two weeks during 1963.The-reducing sugar content of leaves increased with increasing rates of fertilization. In stems and stolons as well as in roots and rhizomes no significant changes occurred in reducing sugar content throughout the growth 'Season. In the leaves there were no significant differences in content of sucrose and fructosan due to fertilizer application but in stems and stolons as well as in rhizomes and roots, sucrose and fructosan content decreased with increasing fertilization.Bermudagrass fertilized at the high rate apparently retains most of the newly synthesized carbohydrate as reducing sugar in'the leaves. The amount of carbohydrate translocated into rhizomes at the-high-nitrogen level is a small fraction of the total amount synthesized. During theactive growth phase, sucrose may be equally as important a source of reserve for regrowth as fructosan.The second phase of the project concerned the evaluation of regrowth potential of the plots fertilized during the first study. Six-inch diameter sod plugs were taken from each plot, put in cans, and grown in a dark chamber. The regrowth potential was measured in mg of dry matter produced per sod plug.The first six-week regrowth was closely related to the content of carbohydrate reserve present in the stubble and rhizome. Sod plugs from plots fertilized at 500 lb. N per acre made the best regrowth. The least regrowth was made by sod plugs from plots fertilized at 750 and 1000 lb. N per acre.The final phase of work involved an evaluation of forage quality of coastal Bermudagrass hays from plots fertilized at 0, 100, and 250 lb. N per acre every six weeks. Rabbits were used as test animals. The grass hays replaced the 40%. alfalfa hay normally incorporated into the control ration. Three feeding experiments were carried out using three successive hay harvests. Feed evaluations were based on the live weight gains of young rabbit from age 21 days to 52 days. In the third experiment 8-week-old rabbits were used and the grass feeds were supplemented with preformed rased vitamin A.In the first two feeding experiments, alfalfa ration was superior to the three coastal Bermudagrass rations, possibly due to the former's higher content of carotene and low level of nitrate. The rabbits fed Bermudagrass rations showed acute symptoms of vitamin A deficiency, masking any observable differences between the coastal Bermudagrass  feeds. La the third experiment, rabbits on fertilized Bermudagrass rations performed very poorly. These rations contained levels of nitrate-nitrogenthat are possibly toxic to rabbits, and which might interfere with availability and utilization of vitamin A.|Theses collection|Nitrogen Fertilization / Forage Quality and Regrowth Potential of CoastalBermudagrass / (Cynodon Dactylon (L) Pers.)*||||||Mbufong, Paul Kuban|Male|A linguistic study of the language of law||||||M. The least degradation was obtained in the presence of 5%w/v polysorbate 80.The effect of compound tragacanth powder and tragacanth mucilage on the stability of aqueous aspirin suspension was also separately determined. O.5%w/v of compound tragacanth powder gave the best stabilizing effect. The rate of hydrolysis of the latter product was monitored as a function of temperature. Aqueous aspirin suspension without surfactant and tragacanth was used as control. The result showed increased degradation of aspirin with increase in temperature.An incorporation of a flavouring agent, a colourant and a preservative in the suspension had no significant influence on the rate of aspirin degradation.Finally, an estimated shelf-life of the aspirin suspension was made based on elevated temperaturestudy. An examination of the performance of the Local Government institutions in South-Western Nigeria, between 1960 and 1980 revealed a skewed orientation of activities and expenditure patterns of councils in favour of services which reinforce an urbanised approach to the problems of the rural areas, a relative rural neglect and a peculiar buck-passing.By em cloying a system model for analysing the rural economy of South-Western Nigeria, it was evident that there is a compelling "urban bias" in the activities. Also, the patterns of rural-urban relation suggest a peculiarity which questions any uniform pattern of local government activities. In the bid to explain these observable features and relative governmental rural ineffectiveness, even among rural councils, it was evident that the predominance of urban ways of life is relatively constraining to rural development. This urban-outlook had however been reinformed by various inter-governmental issues and a seeming buck-passing characteristic of federal systems of government. These various factors have set major limits on the sizes, contents, directions and the relevance of council activities, given the identified problems of the rural areas.While the study argues that Local Governments have performed significant roles in the rural areas in the provision of certain social services and road infrastructure, it is also noted that council-provided-services were the only visible indications of government presence in most localities. But at the same time, most councils were found to be less active in pursuing policies and programmes that are both truly 'local' and relatively - specific to most rural areas.This study calls attention to the various issues and problems facing Local Governments. It argues that the potential for more council effectiveness and efficiency is present in South-Western Nigeria. It also suggests that more Local Government involvement in rural development activities particularly in the salient areas of rural economic activities especially in agriculture will go a long way to creating the needed mechanisms for smooth rural development intermediation.|Theses collection|Local Government Institution / Rural Development*||||||Adesulu,|Male||||||||||Ile-Ife||1984|||OAU||||||||||||English||Obafemi Awolowo University, H. Results of the resistivity data show that the foundation materials have apparent resistivity values below 200 Ohm-metres, The low values are attributable to the porosity, degree of saturation and matrix content of the formation. The seismic refraction results show that the area is underlain by a medium to high quality foundation material (Vp = 2500 m/s), The region with velocity higher than 2500 m/s has an unconfined compressive strength higher than 8.5 x 106 kg/m2 indicating a fairly good foundation rock correlating with fresh sandstone rock.The coefficient of permeability of the sandstone rock varies from 3.10 x 10-6 m/s to  7.95 x 10-6 m/s. Permeability is invariably low in the tar horizons while the tranamissivity and permeability values are high in the artesian aquifers. A total of 40 untrained subjects participated in the study. Subjects were randomly assigned to one of four study groups: (i) Control, (ii) Experimental (1.6 kilometer joggers), (iii) Experimental (3.2 kilometer joggers), (iv) Experimental (4.8 kilometer joggers). There were ten subjects in each study group. The training groups were made to jog the prescribed distances at about 85 percent HRmax, three times a week for 12 weeks.Subjects anthropometric and biochemical measurements were taken through standardized procedures before and after the training programme. A one-way ANOVA was computed on the difference scores which were obtained by subtracting the post from the pre-training scores, for each subject and for each dependent variable. Newman-Keul's post hoc analyses were computed where F-ratio was significant (I< 0.05).The following results were obtained:(i) The exercise groups did not differ significantly from one another with respect to levels of reduction in percent body fat. Percent body fat reduced significantly (P< 0.05) in the exercise groups as compared to the control group.(ii)	In subjects of the 4.8 kilometer group blood glucose level declined significantly (P& 0.05) as compared to those of other groups.(iii)	Subjects in the 3.2 kilometer group had significantly (P< 0.05) lowered level of serum triglyceride than subjects in the other training groups.(iv)	Subjects within the experimental groups generally had greater but insignificant decline in blood pressure, serum cholesterol and serum uric acid levels as compared to the control subjects.It was concluded that jogging over 4.8 kilometers three times a week, for 12 weeks was generally most effective in lowering the levels of coronary risk factors in the group of male undergraduates. This study is divided into six chapters. Chapter one discusses the concepts of adult education generally byreviewing existing definitions and assumptions.  Chapter two examines the various aspects of the informal and formal patterns and the content of the indigenous Yoruba adult education which embraced community consciousness, common values and skills needed for the survival of the society as well as individual vocational enterprises. The third chapter analyses the historical and religious aspects of the establishment and provision of western-style adult education by the Missionaries, traders and government officials as agencies between 1842 and 1882. The religious, commercial and political activities of these agencies provided the basis for the comparative study. The fourth chapter contains an examination of the establishment of Industrial Education. During the 1880's, the Missionaries attempted to modernise the indigenous crafts and vocational training of the Yoruba converts through the apprenticeship system. They adopted for most of their educational programmes the trial-and-error method. In varying degrees of successes and failures, the industrial education programme helped totrain a few Yoruba workers in different occupations like carpentry, masonry, brick making and even farming. Chapter five highlights. the auspicious application of western-style adult education to the agro-economic and social welfare of the Yoruba people. This was brought about by the generalpolitical awareness among the educated Yoruba people which, from 1893 to 1945, led to schism in the C.M.S. The newly established African Churches in the interior of Yorubaland promoted western-style adult education, while chapter six summarises the study and relates the findings and conclusions to the melting point between the indigenous and the western-style adult education systems in Yorubaland.|Theses collection|Yoruba indigenous adult education systems /  western-style adult education systems / Adult education *||||||Adegbulu, Adetoye|Male|RELATIONS BETWEEN NIGERIA AND ANGOLA, 1975 - 1978||||||M. Petrographic studies included thin section study, ignition loss, chemical analysis and x - ray Diffraction. Chemical analysis showed that the samples are hydrous aluminosilicates with appreciable iron titanium and magnesium content. Results from x - ray Diffraction indicated the presence of three groups of minerals, quartz, iron - and clay minerals. The iron minerals are goethite and chamosite while the clay minerals are chlorite, chloriteripidolite and chlorite - montmorillonite.The samples possess an average bulk density of 2.61gm/cc, exhibited medium porosity (10%) .and. specific ,gravity. (2.77). laboratory weathering tests carried out are free swell, water absorption, slake durability and crystallization test. These tests provide a simple, rapid but reliable evaluation of the weatherability and durability of the argillites. The results show a low free swell, average11% and a relative high potential to water absorption, (49%).The samples crumbled easily and are unsound.Possible problems such as swelling ground, squeezing ground and running ground associated with underground construction in generally incompetent rocks were identified. These can be prevented by treatment of materials with chemicals or by allowing the rocks to move under controlled conditions with installation of strain guages.Thus even with these unfavourable engineering properties, the construction of underground structures for winning the coal in the argillites, is still a justifiable engineering feat.|Theses collection|weatherability  / Coal-bearing argillite*||||||Sofekun, Morounfayo Oluwatoyin|Female|An investigation of the ability of environmental bacteria to proliferate in selected intravenous fluids.||||||M. Tunde|Male|An analysis of policy-making and implementation on the Federal (Military) Government's Universal Primary Education Scheme||||||M. P. A. Public Administration|||Ile-Ife, Nigeria |Obafemi Awolowo University, Public Administration|1983||| OAU|||||v, 90p.|||||||English||Obafemi Awolowo University, H. O. Library, Ile-Ife, Osun State. E-mail: ul@library.oauife.edu.ng|http://library.oauife.edu.ng||||I hereby authorize the Hezekiah Oluwasanmi Library to copy my thesis in whole or in part in response to request from individual researchers and organizations for the purpose of private study or research|The Universal Primary Education Scheme under the Federal Military Government was one of the gigantic national efforts which consumed a great deal of the resources of the nation. A close study and analysis of the Policy-making and implementation of the scheme is considered a worthwhile exercise so as to add to the literature that could guide in the formulation and execution of other national efforts.An attempt has been made to trace the genesis of the idea of free education in the whole world in general and in Nigeria in particular. This is followed by an examination of the preparatory planning process, and the policy-making process on the scheme against the background of the Normative Optimum model prescribed by Dror. (1969). Further more, an examination was made of its actual execution by the Bureaucracy, against the background of the Classical School of management as put forward by unwick (1947).From this study, one observes that in the Federal Government's preparation for the U.P.E. Scheme, all the fifteen preparatory steps as enumerated by Dror, for Normative Optimum model, were taken by the Federal Government. The stages were however compliled with in an unco-ordinated 'muddling' fashion charasteristic of Lindblom's Incrementalist approach.This Incrementalist approach was discussed and found unsuitable for the scheme largely because of the time constraint and the novelty of the scheme. The Normative Optimum approach was also found unsuitable becauseof the inadequacy of data, end the unpredictability of our monolithic source of revenue generation. One is therefore compelled to advocate for future schemes, 'the mixed Scanning' approach as enunciated by Amital Etzioni (1963) which combine suitable elements in both the Incrementalist and the Normative optimum models.As far as the actual implementation on the scheme was concerned, it is found that the main constraint is the colonialist oriented bureaucracy. What is therefore recommended is a general re-orientation of the entire Nigerian Bureaucracy towards a more results - oriented Rational Productivity Bureaucracy as advocated by IIchman, {1970), Fredrick Riggs and even by the Udoji Report (1973).|Theses collection|Universal Primary Education*||||||Osundare, Lawrence Akinola|Male|A Design Proposal for the National Orthopaedic Hospital,Lagos, Nigeria||||||M. When the seedlings were heat-stressed at 45C for 16 hours, however, there was a decrease in all of the parameters measured, the rate of decrease being more pronounced with the longer duration of stress in the case of chloroplast formation, leaf length and seedling height. The cowpea seedlings were more sensitive to heat stress than the maize seedlings.When etiolated seedlings of maize were heat-stressed at 45C for 16 hours and then illuminated at 25C, there was a retardation in the rate of accumulation of carotenes and protochlorophyllide, whilethat of xanthophylls, flavones and phytol was enhanced. The accumulation of phytol, however, was reterded in dark-grown seedlings. It is concluded that increased xanthophyll and flavone levels contribute to the heat-induced yellowing of leaves, and that the reduced protochlorophyllide and phytol levels account, at least partly, for the retardation in protochlorophyll accumulation previously reported in heat-stressed seedlings.|Theses collection|heat-stressed seedlings / seedlings of maize and cowpea*||||||Ositelu, Oyenuga O.|Male|Senior Staff Recruitment and Development in the Ogun State Civil Service||||||M. These were evaluated in the context of conventional principles of finished products inventory management, particularly as they relate to marketing planning.The study revealed that the company was faced with an acute problem of managing its stock of finished products, to the extent that it had to rent five additional warehouses at different locations to supplement its on-site storage facilities. The accumulation of stock resulted from inaccuracy of sales estimates; lack of in-depth understanding of customers (and the market generally); inefficiency of the printing department and some external factors which are beyond the company's control.It was observed that this stock accumulation impaired the company's commercial activities. The company should also estimate its customers' stocks of its products. The concentrations of the soaps employed were 0.0625% (w/v), 0.125% (w/v) and 0.25% (w/v). Potassium myristate exhibited the highest reduction of viability of the test organism, followed by Potassium laurate, Potassium palmitate, and lastly Potassium stearate. Antibacterial activity was observed to increase with increasing concentrations of the soaps.Furthermore, the potassium soaps was observed to cause a significant increase in both the nephelometer readings and the optical density of whole cells of the test organisms.The soaps also caused a leakage of intracellular materials. This suggests that soaps have some effect on the cell membrane of bacteria. The leakage induced by potassium myristate was the greatest, while that induced by the stearate was the least. The ability of the soaps to act on the cell membrane was further demonstrated by the uptake of acriflavine in the presence of soaps. E-mail: ul@library.oauife.edu.ng|http://library.oauife.edu.ng||||I hereby authorize the Hezekiah Oluwasanmi Library to copy my thesis in whole or in part in response to request from individual researchers and organizations for the purpose of private study or research|Equity share - ownership is the stock in trade of the capital market whose chief actors are the Stock Exchange, the Securities and Exchange Commission, the Registrars, the Stock Brokers, and the financial institutions. However, equity ownership is not in this paper discussed with respect to these institutions, Rather, its focus is on assessing how far equity share-ownership has succeeded in contributing to the independent economic development of Nigeria.It is shown that from the incorporation of the Lagos Stock Exchange in 1960, to the enactment of the Companies Decree in 1968 and the Nigerian Enterprises Promotion Decrees of 1972 and 1977 Nigeria has experienced changes in its economy similar to those which had earlier taken place in the political sphere with political independence in 1960. This was a period when radical opinions were rampant and nationalism pervaded third world countries including many countries in Africa. It was an era "when governments were urged to curb the excesses of foreign monopoly capital so that control over the national economy could pass into the hands of the country's own citizens and that in the absence of indigenous entrepreneurs, large and experienced enough to take over, governments should themselves take over. In Uganda, it resulted in the explusion of Asians; in Ghana, Nigerians and in Kenya, Europeans.In Uganda, Ghana and Kenya, attempts to hand over control of the economy to citizens resulted in the alienation of foreign nationals, and loss of needed expertise.The policies pursued by the Nigerian Government can there-fore be seen as gradualist and conciliatory affording Nigerians unlimited opportunities of business ownership, and at the sametime providing avenues for foreign investment in advanced technology.The result was that Nigeria experienced no disruption in implementing its policies. Rather, Nigeria earned international respect and co-operation.The study also shows that it is not the majority equity ownership of commercial enterprises, the majority membership of the Boards of Directors, nor the financial gains that accrue from ownership that determine the ultimate control of enterprise. Rather, the ability to control enterprise requires the chief actors to comprehend a given technology and to have the management expertise and ability to evolve relevant technologies.The major findings of this paper is that the various achievements of the "enterprises" promotion decrees can be viewed as aids towards the realisation of greater long-term objectives, which should include the evolution of indigenous technology, the emergence of indigenous management personnel, and control of the Board of Directors.|Theses collection|Equity share - ownership / stock in trade / capital market*||||||Adebanjo Afolabi|Male|Studies on the anthracnose disease of water yam (dioscorea alata, L.)||||||M.PHIL.,  Plant  Science|P. The model described applies to incidence of black pod disease in an experimental plot in Ibadan, Nigeria based on the black pod incidence and meteorological factors for the period of March to November 1976.The 3-compartment model, consists of	(1) number of pods available for infection, (2) number of infected pods and (3) number of infected pods above 200cm; where total pod production is a source and number of pods harvested is a sink. The model is conceptualized as a steady-state physical transfer of elements in the plot. The model was driven with rate of infection, which was developed as a linear function of rainfall frequency and proportion of infected pods 200cm above ground surface; after statistical analysis of factors affecting the dispersal and infection processes of inoculum. All input variables were lagged one week. The parameter values for the driving equation were estimated by least squares method, and those of the compartment model were estimated by direct determination from observed data.Computer simulations that could perform computations on weekly time steps were executed on an IBM-360 machine.The simulation results obtained from the model were compared with observed incidence of black pods. In general, the model output compared favourably with observed data.The validation of the model was achieved by applying the model to a different cocoa plot with the same macroclimatic factors over the same period. The simulation output of the model also compared favourably with the observed data.A sensitivity analysis of the model showed that the rate of infection is sensitive to changes in frequency of rainfall and canopy infection; and the model could be used to predict low- and heavy-loss areas of Nigeria.Laboratory studies on the combined effect of temperature and relative humidity on the length of time it takes for the disease to appear were undertaken. It was found that the lower humidities (less than 80%) and higher humidities (greater than 85%) delay the appearance of the disease even at favourable temperatures (23--25C). It was also noted that higher humidities (equal to or greater than 90%` were favourable for sporulation.|Theses collection|computer model / cocoa black pod disease*||||||Haastrup Adedeji|Male|The Status of Instructional Media in the Teaching of Biology in Selected Secondary Schools in Oyo State of Nigeria||||||M. With a population of 9,487,525 (1963 Census)', and covering about 30,000 square miles, it is mainly an agricultural State whose vegetation falls within the normal tropical pattern.The State's economy is very vulnerable being dependent to a very large extent on cocoa, of which it is the second largest producer in the world. Mitotic selection, fluorodeoxyuridine (FdU) and hydroxyurea (HU) blocks were techniques used for synchronization.Cells that were labeled with 3H-thymidine for a short period of time (10 - 20 minutes) at the beginning or at the end of one S phase were given a density label by providing bromodeoxyuridine (BrdU) at both early and late periods of a subsequent S phase. In CsCl density gradients, a shift of the initial 3H label to the hybrid density was used as measure of the amount of correlation in phase regulated replication of the DNA.The percent 3H or 14C shifted with the density labeled, newly formed hybrid showed that there is a good degree of temporal correlation between DNA's synthesized in the earlyportion of any two S phases and likewise for the DNAreplicated at the end of any two S phases. The results of the CsCl centrifugation also revealed that DNA synthesizedin the early part of any S phase has a higher bouyant density than the average for total DNA, while DNA replicated late in the S phase banded in a position indicating a lower bouyant density (lower G+C/A+T ratio) than native DNA.Hydroxyapatite was also used to separate DNA's synthesized early and late in the S phase into highly repetitive and non-repetitive fractions. In addition, by using hydroxyapatite chromatography it was found that the highly repetitive DNA isolated from the DNA synthesized in the first ten mintes of an S phase contained a higher proportion of G+C sequences than the remaining DNA. The highly repetitive fraction isolated from DNA synthesized late in the S phase had a base composition indistinguishable from total DNA. The non-repetitive DNA sequences isolated from DNA's synthesized in both early and late S phase have base composition similar to the total DNA.The information obtained from the density labeling experiments and hydroxyapatite chromatography, when integrated with related findings, suggest that certain G+C rich sequences preferentially replicated at the beginning of the S phase are either structural entities in the initiation complex for DNA synthesis or structural genes that are preferentially synthesized in the early part of the S phase.|Theses collection|Programming of DNA Synthesis / Nature of DNA Synthesized at Different Times / S Phase of the Cell Cycle of a Eucaryotic System*||||||Adegoke Joseph Adeleke|Male|Comparison of the Base Compositions of the Highly Repetitive, the Intermediate Repetitive and Non-Repetitive DNA of Chinese Hamster Cells||||||1972|J. The result of the survey shows that the present basis for grouping of housing sites and contracts produce unsatisfactory operation; that the current planning tool and control techniques are inadequate for repetitive housing construction with scattered sites and contracts, which in some cases, involves different house types and starting periods; that there is abscence of coordinated policy, in the firms, in guiding efforts for optimal use of resources as sites and contracts get scattered; that overtrading and poorfinancial management, in addition, to delay in measurement of and payment for certified works create liquidity problem for the firms.Company and site organisations which are haphazard show two broad management control practices among the firms. In one, work progresses from one completed housing cluster to the other. Here, labour force is not continuously employed, resulting in delays in converging and dispersing the workers. In the other, work progresses for all clusters in a contract at once. Here, scarce physical and managerial resources are duplicated.Bearing in mind the absence of a rational management system for dealing with mass housing construction on scttered sites, the study suggests a practice. In the practice, physical separation of the housing clusters, housing typology and timing of individual contract with respect to ongoing contracts are emphasized in planning and controlling operations. Adaptive morphology of the alimentary canal was studied.The results show that the time of feeding was between .6 a.m. and 8 p.m. daily with no feeding during the hours of the night. During the day however, there were evidence of variation in feeding intensity with time, with the peak period of feeding lying between 1 p.m. and 5 p.m.	Hydrogen ion concentration along the gut was between 1.1 and 9.5, with the stomach maintaining an acid state while the intestine was alkaline.The nature of the food of S. galilaeus varied with size of fish,	Thus the fry fed mostly on zooplankton, while the juveniles and adults fed on phytoplankton. Forty-seven planktonic genera were identified in the stomach of the fish, and these showed marked seasonal variation.Green algae were predominant between January and April. Diatoms were taken between May and July, while blue-green algae were the main plankton in the diet for the rest ofthe year. The food contained normal ranges of carbohydrates, proteins, lipids, crude fibre and essential mineral elements common in fish diets. Twenty amino acids, including the ten indispensable ones for fishes were detected when food taken from the gut was analysed. Phospholipids, fatty acids and triglycerides were present in the food. On the other hand, sterols (cholesterol and cholesterol esters) were found to be synthesized by the fish. Crude fibreswere very low in the diets of all sizes of fish. The concentration of protein was very high in food of the young, but decreased in diets of larger fish. The nutritional factors of the diet vary with seasons of the year and with fish size.Common gut enzymes include carbohydrases, pro-Leases and lipases. Amylase occurred throughout the length of the gut. Maltase was found only in the adult fish. Pancreatic tissues were found to be the richest source of lipid digesting enzymes. Region I of the intestine which represents the first  of this part of the gut, was the major sites of digestion in the fish.The absorptive capacity of different section of the gut varied. Region II of the intestine was the major site of absorption in the fish. The percentage of different food absorbed varied. Region III of the intestine was responsible for water absorption in the fish.The morphology of the alimentary canal was similar to those of other herbivores, with characteristic long intestine. The intestine consists of three regions identified by colour variations.	These regions also varied in length.|Theses collection|Nutrition in Sarotherodon galilaeus/ Fish*||||||Oforah Chukwudi Cyprian|Male|STUDIES ON RETROGRADATION OF STARCHES OF YAM (Dioscorea rotundata), COCOYA.M(Xanthosoma sagittifolium), AND CASSAVA Manihot utilissima)||||||M. The starches were gelatinized after pH adjustment with hydrochloric acid or ammonium hydroxide, pH values range from 2 to 10 at 1 unit interval. The extent of retrogradation of 8% starch pastes on ageing at room temperature was determined by measuring the optical density of starch-iodine complex in an aqueous supernatant. This is indicative of the cold water solubility of ageing starch molecules. Cassava starch showed least retrogradation at pH 4.o while yam and cocoyam starches showed least retrogradation at pH 6.0. This was attributed to the formation of starch molecules of least retrogradation tendency through fragmentation. An attempt was also made to control retrogradation in yam flour, cocoyam flour, and gari. Raw yam tubers were diced and soaked in citrate buffer, pH 6.0 (prepared from citric acid and sodium citrate) for 10 minutes, steam-blanchedfor 20 minutes and dried at 70C to 135 moisture content. The product obtained retrograded less rapidly than that obtained by soaking in pyrophosphate buffer pH 6.0 (prepared from tetrasodium pyrophosphate and orthophosphoric acid) or sodium metabisulphite pH 6.0 (prepared from sodium metabisulphite and sodium sulphite). This was attributed to the positions of the anions in the Hofmeister series and slight esterification of starch molecules by citrate ions. Cocoyam processed similarly showed least retrogradation with the application of pyrophosphate buffer, pH 6.0. Gari sprayed with pyrophosphate buffer, pH 4.0 (prepared from tetrasodium pyrophosphate and orthophosphoric acid) to 38 % moisture content and dried at 70C to 12% moisture content retrograded less rapidly than the control.|Theses collection|Retrogradation of starches of yam/ Cocoyam/ Cassava*||||||Afolabi Michael Oluwole|Male|Labour Turnover in a Publishing Firm CKC Press (Nigeria) Ltd.
